  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c13ffaaf-042f-48a0-a75f-44dbd8d9b506'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText12851525899388869236" style="display:none">A thrilling story about friendship, loyalty, and revenge<br /><br />When he was outcast, Torak was the hunted one. Nine moons later he becomes the hunter when he vows to avenge the killing of one of his closest friends. Racked by guilt and grief, he follows the killer into the Deep Forest, where the World Spirit stalks the hidden valleys as a tall man with the antlers of a stag. But there is a rottenness at the heart of the Forest, for its clans have succumbed to the lies of the Soul-Eaters. Here, Torak must face fire, war, and overwhelming evil. Oath Breaker is a story about keeping promises and the true cost of vengeance.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2799363851025285051">Torak’s adventures with Wolf, Renn and the other Open Forest clans are endangered by Thiazzi’s reach for power in the Deep Forest where he manipulates the mysterious Red Deer and Auroch clans. In this penultimate volume of the wonderful Wolr Brother series, Torak once again learns about bravery, friendship and forgiveness while nearly losing everything he values. I find that these books are wonderful in their depiction of the Stone Age / Bronze Age in northern Europe and especially loved a momen</span>
  <span id="freeText2799363851025285051" style="display:none">Torak’s adventures with Wolf, Renn and the other Open Forest clans are endangered by Thiazzi’s reach for power in the Deep Forest where he manipulates the mysterious Red Deer and Auroch clans. In this penultimate volume of the wonderful Wolr Brother series, Torak once again learns about bravery, friendship and forgiveness while nearly losing everything he values. I find that these books are wonderful in their depiction of the Stone Age / Bronze Age in northern Europe and especially loved a moment towards the end with the Forest Horses.<br />A must for you and your kids!</span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53101770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12985201234163206353">This is the best book so far in this very good series! It is packed full of adventure, literally from page one! Torak suffers yet another great loss in life, and this time, not being a small child, he swears revenge. He drags those who love him - Wolf, Renn, Fen-Keddin - along on his quest, and often, in spite of the evidence directly in front of him, he allows his oath of vengance to lead him down paths that are not in his best interests. Like any kid feeling grown while not yet being grown, he</span>
  <span id="freeText12985201234163206353" style="display:none">This is the best book so far in this very good series! It is packed full of adventure, literally from page one! Torak suffers yet another great loss in life, and this time, not being a small child, he swears revenge. He drags those who love him - Wolf, Renn, Fen-Keddin - along on his quest, and often, in spite of the evidence directly in front of him, he allows his oath of vengance to lead him down paths that are not in his best interests. Like any kid feeling grown while not yet being grown, he takes on too much blame for things not really his fault and not enough for things that are - and still, Renn and Wolf stick with him. They all grow and learn edge towards a better life. There is much else I'd like to write, but one thing leads to another, and I don't want to give anything away. <br /><br />I'd recommend this series to kids of any age, only pausing to phrase my recommendation with a disclaimer that this series takes place in an imagined world, 6000 years ago. We don't really know how folks lived, or what they thought supplied the life force that obviously surrounds them - if your own belief structure is so shaky you can't contemplate a world of clans, bonded to animal spirits and living lives filled with mysticism and inexplicable events without endangering your own spiritual well being - - - then sorry. Go re-read the Chronicles of Narnia (yawn). </span>
  <a data-text-id="12985201234163206353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_119387735" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119387735" />
    <a title="CaroleHeidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3909842-caroleheidi"><img alt="CaroleHeidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490737211p2/3909842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119387735?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CaroleHeidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CaroleHeidi" href="/user/show/3909842-caroleheidi">CaroleHeidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119387735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10939161028075565867">What I liked: Where to start? I have loved this series of books since I first opened Wolf Brother in 2004. Michelle Paver’s beautiful writing creates an ancient world that instantly draws you in and makes you believe in it so much you can almost feel the breeze and hear the Forest leaves rustling around you.<br/><br/>I love her detail. She has obviously done a lot of research and truly immersed herself in the world of post-ice age Europe and this reflects in every single line of the book. You can tell she</span>
  <span id="freeText10939161028075565867" style="display:none">What I liked: Where to start? I have loved this series of books since I first opened Wolf Brother in 2004. Michelle Paver’s beautiful writing creates an ancient world that instantly draws you in and makes you believe in it so much you can almost feel the breeze and hear the Forest leaves rustling around you.<br /><br />I love her detail. She has obviously done a lot of research and truly immersed herself in the world of post-ice age Europe and this reflects in every single line of the book. You can tell she has spent days at the UK Wolf Conservation Trust watching how the wolves move and act around each other, you can tell she’s visited Polish forests untouched by human hands and all of that adds up to make these some of the best young teen novels I have ever read in terms of world building and realism.<br /><br />Her characters are brilliant also. Surprisingly easy to relate to despite living lives so different from our own, just a few pages in it feels ‘normal’ to leave a scrap of food in a tree fork as a ‘thank you’ to the Forest for providing or making sure your bow is carefully oiled and always ready to use. Torak is strong-willed and one of my favourite characters in any book, partly because of his close relationship to Wolf and partly because he is so very human in his doubts, passion and fears.<br /><br />The story is fast paced and exciting, keeping you turning the pages long after you should have switched off the light and gone to sleep or stopped reading to do your homework.<br /><br />What I didn’t like: This is much harder to answer because there is nothing I can come up with to dislike. Which means Michelle must be doing something very right indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10939161028075565867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer998349518295305364">This wasn't the best of Michelle Paver's books in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series. There were quite a lot of parts in the book that lacked believability for me. Since I work with horses, I felt a big ouch there and wished she had done better research on them. However, it was an exciting read. As always, she has a writing style that really draws you in. The theme of the struggle against a need for revenge was the best aspect of the book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2877548111" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63824806-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484326813p2/63824806.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2877548111?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/63824806-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2877548111&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2877548111" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16016255434911138419">Torak’s world is one of my favourite places to visit when reading a fantasy book series and my reread of book 5 as an adult was everything I hoped it would be and more.<br/><br/>After having spent several moons as an outcast, the clans have taken Torak back following the exposure and defeat of Seshru the Viper Mage. Two pieces of the Fire Opal have now been destroyed, but the third and final piece is in the islands, where Torak and his friends must journey to retrieve it before the two remaining Soul Eate</span>
  <span id="freeText16016255434911138419" style="display:none">Torak’s world is one of my favourite places to visit when reading a fantasy book series and my reread of book 5 as an adult was everything I hoped it would be and more.<br /><br />After having spent several moons as an outcast, the clans have taken Torak back following the exposure and defeat of Seshru the Viper Mage. Two pieces of the Fire Opal have now been destroyed, but the third and final piece is in the islands, where Torak and his friends must journey to retrieve it before the two remaining Soul Eaters can do so. They may already be too late however and the resulting consequences catastrophic.<br /><br />When I first read Oathbreaker, I blitzed through it without paying much attention to the level of detail Paver addresses throughout her world. I was overly keen to see outcome of Torak’s struggle. Now on my reread, I can appreciate the extent she went to conjure such a vivid and rich world derived from own experiences in deep forest country, which is where the majority of Oathbreaker is set. So much so it makes me want to experience the beauty of the areas Paver visited for writing Oathbreaker myself by visiting them at some point.<br /><br />One of the strongest aspects of book 5 was the return of Thiazzi. Having reread Soul Eater earlier this year I saw him as an even nastier antagonist than on my first experience with the man. Upon his return he becomes a much more involved character and some of his acts I am surprised to find written in YA/children’s series because they were simply horrific.<br /><br />Another stellar novel by Paver which merits a full 5 stars, onto the finale of the original 6 books Ghosthunter before I buy my copy of the new novel Viper’s Daughter scheduled for 2020. I am so happy Paver decided to write more novels set in this world and have no doubt her future novels will be as good as the originals!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16016255434911138419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2782473579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2782473579" />
    <a title="Jennie Louwes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89985522-jennie-louwes"><img alt="Jennie Louwes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584340118p2/89985522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2782473579?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennie Louwes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennie Louwes" href="/user/show/89985522-jennie-louwes">Jennie Louwes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2782473579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3329833667566584328">"Some places hold an echo of events; others possess their own spirit." (Oath Breaker, page 140)<br/><br/>Each book within "The Ancient Chronicles of Darkness" is filled with truth and wisdom wrapped within fiction. <br/><br/>Each book stands on its own, while being interwoven with the one standing next to it; and, each book draws you in. <br/><br/>"Oath Breaker" receives a 4 star rating only because the list of new clans introduced creates a bit of a muddle. From start to finish, the waters ran a bit muddy and slowed things </span>
  <span id="freeText3329833667566584328" style="display:none">"Some places hold an echo of events; others possess their own spirit." (Oath Breaker, page 140)<br /><br />Each book within "The Ancient Chronicles of Darkness" is filled with truth and wisdom wrapped within fiction. <br /><br />Each book stands on its own, while being interwoven with the one standing next to it; and, each book draws you in. <br /><br />"Oath Breaker" receives a 4 star rating only because the list of new clans introduced creates a bit of a muddle. From start to finish, the waters ran a bit muddy and slowed things down for me.<br /><br />You can easily track characters without confusion. It's just that for all of Michelle Paver's exquisite technique and sharing of detail, (which typically allows a reader to be one within its pages, living and breathing next to its main characters); this time, the descriptives got in the way a bit for me.<br /><br />A magnificent read, nonetheless; more tightly held secrets are revealed to include information previously unknown about Torak's Fa and Mother along with why his Mom declared him to be without a clan. <br /><br />The revelations are brilliant.<br /><br />Michelle Paver's series for young adults remains one that none should miss regardless of age or gender. This authoress has lived and breathed alongside her characters too and you can tell. She's just as in love with them as you'll find yourself to be. <br /><br />Bravo Michelle Paver's; Bravo!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3329833667566584328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2234278-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240083607p2/2234278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55314995?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/2234278-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060728373" href="/book/show/5286903-oath-breaker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55314995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3899336437751750145">CHRONICLE OF ANCIENT DARKNESS - BOOK 5: OATH BREAKER by Michelle Paver<br/>Oath Breaker is about a boy who lived in prehistoric times and had to learn to survive on his own. His father has died and he has been outcast from any clan. When Torak's best friend is killed, he swears vengence and goes after the killer along with another best friend and her uncle. I loved how the author enabled us to see what life was like back then and to see how people saw and interpreted their world. It was fascinating h</span>
  <span id="freeText3899336437751750145" style="display:none">CHRONICLE OF ANCIENT DARKNESS - BOOK 5: OATH BREAKER by Michelle Paver<br />Oath Breaker is about a boy who lived in prehistoric times and had to learn to survive on his own. His father has died and he has been outcast from any clan. When Torak's best friend is killed, he swears vengence and goes after the killer along with another best friend and her uncle. I loved how the author enabled us to see what life was like back then and to see how people saw and interpreted their world. It was fascinating how well they could communicate with the animals--both human and animal understood &amp; befriended one another. But, at the same time, I had a hard time wrapping my mind around the idea that humans could actually learn and speak the audible language of animals. However, it was easy to believe you were actually there, in the wild, having to fight to survive. The names that the author used in the book were a bit confusing, at times. Was that a person's name? Was that the name of a Clan? Or was that the name of something in nature? But I eventually caught on to the system. I thoroughly enjoyed this book and I'd recommend it to anyone who loves to read about prehistoric cultures. And even though I was able to understand everything in this book, I think reading the first four books would help you learn about the naming system and how the humans &amp; animals could communicate, among other things about this culture.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3899336437751750145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824755026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8222981544451904331">"Sometimes there's no warning. Nothing at all."<br/><br/>I am so in love with these books. I don't even know what to say about this, the 5th book in the "Chronicles of Ancient Darkness". AMAZING once again. I was so sad to see Bale go, but the ending of this book made up for so much. It really brought a tear to my eye. How special the relationships formed throughout this series have been. Wolf and Torak and Renn…just incredible. The chemistry between all the characters and their individual personalities a</span>
  <span id="freeText8222981544451904331" style="display:none">"Sometimes there's no warning. Nothing at all."<br /><br />I am so in love with these books. I don't even know what to say about this, the 5th book in the "Chronicles of Ancient Darkness". AMAZING once again. I was so sad to see Bale go, but the ending of this book made up for so much. It really brought a tear to my eye. How special the relationships formed throughout this series have been. Wolf and Torak and Renn…just incredible. The chemistry between all the characters and their individual personalities are so well crafted. I could read these books over and over again. I cannot say enough good things…these stories are original and thoughtful and full of absolute wonder. Thanks again to my special friend Matic for recommending such a "goodread" &lt;3<br /><br />"She was tired and stiff from the crossing, and hollow with grief, and lonely. She hadn't known she could be so lonely among people she loved."<br /><br />"Yes, but it's more than that. This is the cubs first time ever out of the Den. That's the most important day of all, because it's when they meet the rest of the pack. With a wave of his hand, he took in Wolf and his mate and the cubs, and Renn and himself. The rest of the pack, he said again. That's us."<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText4212668234248792789" style="display:none">Just like the first four books in this series, Michelle Paver keeps the action and adventure fast-paced and gripping. We follow Torak into the Deep Forest where danger threatens him at every turn as he seeks to fulfill his oath of vengenance against one of the Soul Eaters. Ms. Paver's beautiful writing is such that we can feel his despair and anger and pain as though it were our own. I think that what I like most about this series is the incredible bond between Torak and Wolf. They are pack-brothers and, despite outside forces that try to tear them apart, they share a deep loyalty and love for one another that can never be destroyed. Ms. Paver has done a lot of research on wolf behaviour and it definitely shows in her writing. Only one more book left in the series and I will be sad to see the adventure end!</span>

<div id="review_2192092073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2192092073" />
    <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler"><img alt="Brittney Tyler" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2192092073?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney Tyler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney Tyler" href="/user/show/56506626-brittney-tyler">Brittney Tyler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060728373" href="/book/show/5286903-oath-breaker">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a fun read!!!!!!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56506626-brittney-tyler?shelf=personal-library">personal-library</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2192092073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16029556397140212482">Star Rating: 5 stars<br/><br/>Note: This is the 5th book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br/><br/>I picked up Oath Breaker by Michelle Paver because I needed a shorter book to complete my reading goal, but I ended up thoroughly enjoying this one because it fixed a lot of problems that I had with the previous two books as it filled in a lot of the plot holes. I actually ended up reading the entire book in one day, which I haven’t done in a really long time. <br/><br/>As al</span>
  <span id="freeText16029556397140212482" style="display:none">Star Rating: 5 stars<br /><br />Note: This is the 5th book in the Chronicles of Ancient Darkness series so this will not be an in-depth review. <br /><br />I picked up Oath Breaker by Michelle Paver because I needed a shorter book to complete my reading goal, but I ended up thoroughly enjoying this one because it fixed a lot of problems that I had with the previous two books as it filled in a lot of the plot holes. I actually ended up reading the entire book in one day, which I haven’t done in a really long time. <br /><br />As always, we got to learn about a new area of this world, and this time it is the Deep Forest, and that was as interesting as always. However, the one thing that made this book stand out was the plot-holes that got filled in about the rise of the Soul Eaters, how Torak’s parents became involved, and why Torak is so important and why he is the only one who can finish the destruction of the Soul Eaters that his parents started. I am really glad that Paver used this book to fill in most of the plot holes, as there was so many that I was starting to lose interest in the series, and this is the reason why I enjoyed this book almost as much as the 1st one. <br /><br />I also appreciated how this book focused on war, how different people react to it, and how it should be avoided at all cost because of the damage and strife it causes. As many books centers around an epic war, I appreciated how this book focuses on the better concept of trying to avoid war as it tends to tear society and the people involved apart. I loved that Paver took a fresher perspective than most other authors in this genre did. <br /><br />All in all, this was a great addition to this series, and I can’t wait to finish it. 5 stars and a major improvement from the last couple ones in this series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16029556397140212482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_874257877" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/874257877" />
    <a title="Mija " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29388221-mija"><img alt="Mija " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504018573p2/29388221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/874257877?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mija " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mija " href="/user/show/29388221-mija">Mija </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29388221-mija?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer874257877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3126138337842458324">Couldn’t be anything less than 5 stars. This series is just so good, so meaningful. <br/><br/>The trend of clear warnings/lessons continues, as Torak learns that he cannot let vengeance rule him... and also primarily not to separate from his friends and leave them when he gets angry! He is pursued by soul-eaters, you’d think he’d consider this, but alas. <br/><br/>I just love the themes of family — of finding a ‘mate’ (Wolf and Darkfur, I mean how sweet) and one’s own ‘pack.’ The way that Michelle Paver reveals to </span>
  <span id="freeText3126138337842458324" style="display:none">Couldn’t be anything less than 5 stars. This series is just so good, so meaningful. <br /><br />The trend of clear warnings/lessons continues, as Torak learns that he cannot let vengeance rule him... and also primarily not to separate from his friends and leave them when he gets angry! He is pursued by soul-eaters, you’d think he’d consider this, but alas. <br /><br />I just love the themes of family — of finding a ‘mate’ (Wolf and Darkfur, I mean how sweet) and one’s own ‘pack.’ The way that Michelle Paver reveals to us how much Renn and Torak mean to each other is very clever (how they gravitate toward each other, how they save each other, their thoughts of the other when they seem unlike themselves, and all the little flashbacks of small moments — like when Torak says that they share everything just like their ravens do). <br /><br />I also realized what I love about the writing style. It feels close in a sense, keeping some of that immediacy of a first-person POV. But it also feels just distant enough to remind you that this should have happened 6000 years ago. In other words, it’s a limited third-person perspective that I just jive with and that works really well. <br /><br />I was also really intrigued by the setting and the setting is something that really makes each book singular, compelling, and memorable — standing out from the series for a particular reason. I may look at trees a little differently than before, just like we learned Torak always does with whatever being he spirit walks in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3126138337842458324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer979492033394536291">Very few times has a book fully emersed me into a world outside of my own, and made me feel curious of what comes next. I'm about to start the last book in the series, Ghost Hunter, but first thought I needed to share my thoughts on this one.<br/><br/>Starting out with Torak visiting Bale, his Seal clan bonekin, turning to a revenge story with friendships strained and war on the horizon.   <span id="freeText979492033394536291" style="display:none">Very few times has a book fully emersed me into a world outside of my own, and made me feel curious of what comes next. I'm about to start the last book in the series, Ghost Hunter, but first thought I needed to share my thoughts on this one.<br /><br />Starting out with Torak visiting Bale, his Seal clan bonekin, turning to a revenge story with friendships strained and war on the horizon. Fin-Keddin being forced back to the clan, Torak and Renn alone in the Deep Forest fighting to survive alone with waring clans all thanks to Thiazzi the Oak Mage.<br /><br />Reading Oath Breaker, you end up feeling Torak's hatred for Thiazzi after having pushed Bale off the edge and swearing an oath that he finds the Mage and gets revenge. Fire spreading to destroy half the forest, Torak's journey between the Aurochs and Forest Horse tribes range being deadly, riding the sacred black mare and breaking his oath to Bale. All ending the way it did leaves you wanting more of the emotional rollercoaster you've just come off of.<br /><br />Wolf found his life mate, and introduced his cubs to his pack leaves a happy tone for the end of all the atrocities Thiazzi commited before his death.</span>

<div id="review_2844611828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2844611828" />
    <a title="Travis Berketa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8307433-travis-berketa"><img alt="Travis Berketa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513776499p2/8307433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2844611828?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Travis Berketa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Travis Berketa" href="/user/show/8307433-travis-berketa">Travis Berketa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842551165" href="/book/show/6957047-oath-breaker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2844611828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2854767902384508770"><b>
  <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness: Oath Breaker</i>
</b> has been the best book in the series so far; whether it's because the characters are now known or whether it is simply a better story, I'm not sure.<br/><br/>I liked the fact that the author, Michelle Paver, did not continue with the usual annoying Torak/Renn interactions that are found in the previous books; where they continually argue about not being told something, when they're each keeping secrets from one another. In this book, we find Torak's kin, Ba</span>
  <span id="freeText2854767902384508770" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness: Oath Breaker</i>
</b> has been the best book in the series so far; whether it's because the characters are now known or whether it is simply a better story, I'm not sure.<br /><br />I liked the fact that the author, Michelle Paver, did not continue with the usual annoying Torak/Renn interactions that are found in the previous books; where they continually argue about not being told something, when they're each keeping secrets from one another. In this book, we find Torak's kin, Bale (found in the second book, <b>
  <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness: Spirit Walker</i>
</b>), is murdered by the Soul Eater Thiassi, who steals the fire opal and decides to hide away in the Deep Forest to plot the destruction of the clans.<br /><br />I liked that Paver goes into more storytelling with Wolf and his bond with Torak, along with the telling of Wolf's own story. She also gives us more information about Torak's mother and why he had to be "<i>clanless</i>" in the eyes of the clans. These new details about the main characters helped flesh them out a bit more and made me begin to feel something for the characters; which I felt was missing in the other four books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2854767902384508770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303020885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14714700742310943426">Okay, I give up. I made it through four of these. The first one, Wolf Brother was good. I especially like the parts of the story told from the wolf's POV. As the series go on, they get progressively darker, and not in a Harry Potter-ish "we are battling a great evil with friends standing beside us" type of way. Well, maybe the writer is suffering from Rowling-itis. Not every children's book makes a great young adult series. All I know is, I could not hand books 2-5 to any of the ten to 12 year o</span>
  <span id="freeText14714700742310943426" style="display:none">Okay, I give up. I made it through four of these. The first one, Wolf Brother was good. I especially like the parts of the story told from the wolf's POV. As the series go on, they get progressively darker, and not in a Harry Potter-ish "we are battling a great evil with friends standing beside us" type of way. Well, maybe the writer is suffering from Rowling-itis. Not every children's book makes a great young adult series. All I know is, I could not hand books 2-5 to any of the ten to 12 year olds in my life, not in good conscious. ****Spoiler alert***** in the first few pages of this book, one of the main characters from book 4, is murdered in a very gruesome way. I put the book down. There is one more book in this series, but I'm tapping out here. I almost tapped out when the animals were tortured and skinned in book 3, but I hoped it would get better. I'm done.</span>

<div id="review_293285184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293285184" />
    <a title="Martina Sanjaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/918505-martina-sanjaya"><img alt="Martina Sanjaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471541383p2/918505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293285184?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martina Sanjaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martina Sanjaya" href="/user/show/918505-martina-sanjaya">Martina Sanjaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293285184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6939578083638510160">Dark as ever, wonderful as usual. Very sad beginning, very nice ending. Now the adventure roamed in the Deep Forest. Wonder where the next place will be, since Torak had practically wandered everywhere, in about 2 years according to the book. Is it possible to travel from mountain to open forest to sea to highest peaks to deep forest in so short a time? Anyway, I don't really care, because this series is so good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2498152926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2498152926" />
    <a title="Johnny Bennett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/554177-johnny-bennett"><img alt="Johnny Bennett" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2498152926?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johnny Bennett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johnny Bennett" href="/user/show/554177-johnny-bennett">Johnny Bennett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060728373" href="/book/show/5286903-oath-breaker">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2498152926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3080244965507850229">More action and better flow make Oath Breaker stand out over other books in the series. More back story gets filled in. More character development. And relationship struggles continue to be a theme. Though how Michelle Paver points out the irritating, self deflating dance humans go through to find and affirm our mates is humorously called out by wolf in this book, perhaps as a nod how frustrating it is in real life. And dumb. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f5ZXSey0yE/U4X1OHcmnX4mc0lL2gAmiXbR5MgdS+xwpyEvHtzQIVpj1+65erE8Q50dWSq4MUa0rSesuRWTmVA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r84som2B814DZNfhQt45SR3iiGqJFYx07hwgl84AgiL5kDAsNgEzR09wUQEBu9EGczkMctGZ1HuY4bKLjDafag==')})
  }

Better tomorrow than today.&quot; Harder work means the citizens of Aramanth can keep moving forward to improved life stations--from Gray tenements and Orange apartments, upwards to glorious mansions of White. Only some families, like the Haths, believe more in ideas and dreams than in endless toil and ratings. When Kestrel Hath decides she is through with the Aramanth work ethic, she is joined in her small rebellion by her twin brother Bowman and their friend Mumpo. Together, they set the orderly city on its ear by escaping Aramanth\'s walls for an adventure that takes them from city sewers to desert sandstorms. Guided by an archaic map, they know that if they can find the voice of the Wind Singer, an ancient and mysterious instrument that stands in the center of Aramanth, they can save their people from their dreamless existence. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12962632665010752485">Michelle Paver was born in Central Africa, but came to England as a child. After gaining a degree in Biochemistry from Oxford University, she became a partner in a City law firm, but eventually gave that up to write full-time.<br/><br/>The hugely successful <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness</i> series arose from Michelle's lifelong passion for animals, anthropology and the distant past - as as well as an encounter</span>
  <span id="freeText12962632665010752485" style="display:none">Michelle Paver was born in Central Africa, but came to England as a child. After gaining a degree in Biochemistry from Oxford University, she became a partner in a City law firm, but eventually gave that up to write full-time.<br /><br />The hugely successful <i>Chronicles of Ancient Darkness</i> series arose from Michelle's lifelong passion for animals, anthropology and the distant past - as as well as an encounter with a large bear in a remote valley in southern California. To research the books, Michelle has traveled to Finland, Greenland, Sweden, Norway, Arctic Canada and the Carpathian Mountains. She has slept on reindeer skins, swum with wild orca (killer whales), and got nose-to-nose with polar bears - and, of course, wolves. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12962632665010752485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
